# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes
**Task Type:** Security Analysis (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a security engineer auditing the Kubernetes API server's RBAC authorization subsystem. Your goal is to trace the complete authorization flow from when an API request arrives to when a permission decision (allow/deny) is made, mapping the attack surface and identifying security controls.

## Your Task

Analyze the Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow and write a comprehensive security analysis. Trace how API requests are authorized, identify entry points where untrusted input enters the authorization decision path, map the data flow through authorization plugins, and assess the security posture of the RBAC implementation.

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Required Sections

### Files Examined
- List each file you analyzed and its role in the RBAC authorization flow

### Entry Points
1. Identify where API requests enter the authorization subsystem
2. Identify where RBAC policy data (roles, bindings) enters the system
3. Note any places where untrusted input could influence authorization decisions

### Data Flow
Trace the authorization flow through these stages:
1. **Request arrival** — HTTP handler receives the request
2. **Authentication** — Request identity is established
3. **Authorization filter** — Request is routed to authorizer chain
4. **RBAC evaluation** — Role and binding resolution, permission check
5. **Decision** — Allow/deny outcome and audit logging

For each stage, name the specific file, function, and data structures involved.

### Dependency Chain
Provide an ordered list of files from request entry to authorization decision.

### Analysis
- What vulnerability classes could apply (auth bypass, privilege escalation, policy misconfiguration)?
- What existing mitigations are in place?
- What are the security boundaries between authorization plugins?
- How does the authorizer chain (RBAC, Node, Webhook) interact?

### Summary
Concise description of the RBAC authorization security posture and key findings.

## Constraints

- **Analysis only** — do NOT modify any source files
- Be specific — include file paths, function names, and type names
- Focus on the `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/` directories

218\t\trequestedUser := headers.Get(authenticationv1.ImpersonateUserHeader)\n   219\t\thasUser := len(requestedUser) > 0\n   220\t\tif hasUser {\n   221\t\t\tif namespace, name, err := Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes API server implements authorization as a multi-layered HTTP middleware pipeline. Every inbound request passes through a deterministic chain of filters before reaching a resource handler. The authorization decision is made by a **union authorizer** that dispatches to an ordered sequence of sub-authorizers (typically: Node \u2192 RBAC \u2192 Webhook). The RBAC sub-authorizer evaluates role bindings against a user's identity, using an additive, allow-list-only model: RBAC can only allow, never explicitly deny.\n\nThis analysis traces the complete flow from TCP packet arrival to final permission grant or denial, examining every data structure, interface, matching algorithm, and security boundary encountered along the way.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Codebase Overview and Key Files\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` | `DefaultBuildHandlerChain()` \u2014 constructs the full middleware stack |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | `WithAuthentication`, `WithImpersonation` \u2014 identity layer |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | `WithAuthorization`, `GetAuthorizerAttributes()` \u2014 gate filter |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request/requestinfo.go` | `RequestInfo`, `RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo()` \u2014 URL parser |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Core interfaces: `Authorizer`, `Attributes`, `Decision` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` `RuleAllows()`, `RulesAllow()` |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go` | `SubjectAccessEvaluator` \u2014 inverse lookup |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/node/node_authorizer.go` | escalation prevention |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/user/user.go` | Well-known user/group constants |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Core Interfaces and Data Structures\n\n### 3.1 Decision Type\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go:174-184\ntype Decision int\nconst (\n    DecisionDeny      Decision = iota  // 0 \u2014 explicit denial (short-circuit stop)\n    DecisionAllow                       // 1 \u2014 explicit allow (short-circuit stop)\n    DecisionNoOpinion                   // 2 \u2014 no opinion; continue to next authorizer\n)\n```\n\nThe three-valued decision type is the foundation of the union dispatch model. `DecisionNoOpinion` is non-terminal; `DecisionAllow` and `DecisionDeny` are terminal. The final response to the client is `403 Forbidden` if and only if no authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` and no authorizer returns `DecisionDeny` first \u2014 because the chain falls through to `NoOpinion` which maps to Forbidden in `WithAuthorization`. A `DecisionDeny` from any single authorizer immediately stops the chain and returns 403.\n\n### 3.2 Authorizer Interface\n\n```go\n// interfaces.go:82-84\ntype Authorizer interface {\n    Authorize(ctx context.Context, a Attributes) (authorized Decision, reason string, err error)\n}\n```\n\nEvery sub-authorizer (Node, RBAC, Webhook, builtins) implements this single method. The `reason` string is propagated to the audit log and to the 403 response body.\n\n### 3.3 Attributes Interface / AttributesRecord\n\n```go\n// interfaces.go:30-77\ntype Attributes interface {\n    GetUser() user.Info         // authenticated identity\n    GetVerb() string            // k8s verb: get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, deletecollection, proxy\n    GetNamespace() string       // target namespace (empty = cluster-scoped)\n    GetResource() string        // resource type, e.g. \"pods\"\n    GetSubresource() string     // e.g. \"status\", \"log\", \"exec\"\n    GetName() string            // specific object name (if present in URL)\n    GetAPIGroup() string        // API group, e.g. \"apps\", \"batch\", \"\" for core\n    GetAPIVersion() string      // API version, e.g. \"v1\"\n    IsResourceRequest() bool    // true for /api/* and /apis/*; false for /healthz, /metrics etc.\n    GetPath() string            // full URL path (for non-resource requests)\n    GetFieldSelector() (fields.Requirements, error)  // selector-aware authz (feature-gated)\n    GetLabelSelector() (labels.Requirements, error)  // selector-aware authz (feature-gated)\n}\n```\n\nThe concrete implementation is `AttributesRecord`, a value struct (no mutex) built by `GetAuthorizerAttributes()` in the `WithAuthorization` filter, combining the user identity from the context with the parsed `RequestInfo`.\n\n### 3.4 user.Info Constants\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/user/user.go\nconst (\n    SystemPrivilegedGroup = \"system:masters\"      // unconditional cluster-admin access\n    NodesGroup            = \"system:nodes\"         // triggers Node authorizer path\n    AllAuthenticated      = \"system:authenticated\" // auto-added for any authenticated user\n    AllUnauthenticated    = \"system:unauthenticated\"\n    Anonymous             = \"system:anonymous\"\n    APIServerUser         = \"system:apiserver\"     // loopback client identity\n    KubeProxy             = \"system:kube-proxy\"\n    KubeControllerManager = \"system:kube-controller-manager\"\n    KubeScheduler         = \"system:kube-scheduler\"\n    MonitoringGroup       = \"system:monitoring\"\n)\n```\n\nThese constants are structurally significant: group membership determines which authorizer path is taken and which bootstrap policy rules apply.\n\n---\n\n## 4. HTTP Handler Chain: Request Entry to Authorization Gate\n\n### 4.1 Handler Chain Construction\n\nThe complete middleware stack is assembled in `DefaultBuildHandlerChain()` (`config.go:1004-1079`). Handlers are stacked in code from innermost to outermost \u2014 meaning they are listed in **reverse** execution order. The middleware wraps each subsequent handler, so the **first handler in the source code list is the last to execute** during request processing.\n\n**Execution order for an incoming request (outermost first):**\n\n```\nInbound Request\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n 1. WithAuditInit               \u2014 allocates AuditContext in request context\n 2. WithPanicRecovery           \u2014 catches panics, emits 500\n 3. WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete \u2014 waits for API registration to complete\n 4. WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\u2014 stamps arrival time on context\n 5. WithRequestInfo             \u2014 parses URL \u2192 RequestInfo; stored in context\n 6. WithLatencyTrackers         \u2014 start latency tracking\n 7. WithTracing (optional)      \u2014 OpenTelemetry span start\n 8. WithHTTPLogging             \u2014 access log\n 9. WithHSTS                    \u2014 Strict-Transport-Security header\n10. WithCacheControl            \u2014 Cache-Control: no-store\n11. WithCORS                    \u2014 CORS preflight handling\n12. WithRetryAfter (optional)   \u2014 429 during graceful shutdown\n13. WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests \u2014 per-request deadline enforcement\n14. WithRequestDeadline         \u2014 audit-aware deadline wrapper\n15. WithWaitGroup               \u2014 tracks in-flight requests for graceful shutdown\n16. WithAuthentication  \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 AUTHENTICATION GATE\n17. WithAudit                   \u2014 evaluates audit policy; wraps ResponseWriter\n18. WithImpersonation  \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 IDENTITY SUBSTITUTION GATE\n19. WithPriorityAndFairness /   \u2014 request concurrency / rate limiting\n    WithMaxInFlightLimit\n20. WithAuthorization  \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 AUTHORIZATION GATE\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n apiHandler (GoRestful / NonGoRestful routing \u2192 resource handler)\n```\n\nThis ordering is architecturally significant:\n\n- **RequestInfo is available before authentication**, so both authn and authz filters can read resource/verb/namespace without re-parsing the URL.\n- **Authentication** (step 16) precedes **Impersonation** (step 18): impersonation requires the original user to be authenticated first, then separately authorized to impersonate.\n- **Audit** (step 17) wraps the response writer before authorization, so the `RequestReceived` audit event is emitted even for requests that are subsequently denied.\n- **Rate limiting** (step 19) sits between impersonation and authorization: resource limiting decisions reference the (possibly impersonated) user identity after it is established.\n- **Authorization** (step 20) is the last security gate before the resource handler. By this point, the request has a fully resolved, audited identity.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Authentication Layer: Identity Establishment\n\n### 5.1 WithAuthentication (`authentication.go:46-125`)\n\n```go\nfunc withAuthentication(handler http.Handler, auth authenticator.Request, failed http.Handler,\n    apiAuds authenticator.Audiences, requestHeaderConfig *authenticatorfactory.RequestHeaderConfig,\n    metrics authenticationRecordMetricsFunc) http.Handler {\n```\n\n**Processing steps:**\n\n1. **Audience injection**: If API audiences are configured, they are placed on the request context before calling the authenticator. Token authenticators validate that the token's intended audience matches.\n\n2. **Authentication call**: `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` dispatches to a union of authenticators (client certificates, bearer tokens, webhook token review, OIDC, etc.). Returns `(resp *authenticator.Response, ok bool, err error)`.\n\n3. **Failure path**: If `!ok` or `err != nil`, the `failedHandler` is invoked. The `failedHandler` chain is:\n   ```\n   Unauthorized() \u2192 WithFailedAuthenticationAudit()\n   ```\n   This emits an audit event with `\"stage\": \"ResponseComplete\"` and `\"responseCode\": 401` before responding.\n\n4. **Audience acceptability check**: `audiencesAreAcceptable()` validates that the token audience and the server's configured audiences have a non-empty intersection. Mismatched audiences produce a 401 without an error log entry that could expose token details.\n\n5. **Credential header stripping**: On successful authentication, the filter strips all credential-carrying headers:\n   - `Authorization` header\n   - Standard proxy headers: `X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Uid`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*`\n   - Custom proxy headers (from `requestHeaderConfig`)\n   \n   This prevents the resource handler layer from accessing raw credentials and stops the headers from being forwarded in proxy scenarios.\n\n6. **HTTP/2 DOS mitigation** (`UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature gate): Anonymous users on HTTP/2 connections receive `Connection: close`, forcing a new TCP connection per request. This mitigates stream-multiplexing abuse (CVE-2023-44487, CVE-2023-39325).\n\n7. **Identity storage**: `req.WithContext(genericapirequest.WithUser(req.Context(), resp.User))` stores `user.Info` on the request context. All subsequent filters and the resource handler read identity from the context, never from request headers.\n\n### 5.2 Loopback Token Registration (`config.go:1159-1184`)\n\n```go\nfunc AuthorizeClientBearerToken(loopback *restclient.Config, authn *AuthenticationInfo, authz *AuthorizationInfo) {\n    privilegedLoopbackToken := loopback.BearerToken\n    var uid = uuid.New().String()\n    tokens := make(map[string]*user.DefaultInfo)\n    tokens[privilegedLoopbackToken] = &user.DefaultInfo{\n        Name:   user.APIServerUser,               // \"system:apiserver\"\n        UID:    uid,                               // random UUID per startup\n        Groups: []string{user.AllAuthenticated, user.SystemPrivilegedGroup},\n    }\n    tokenAuthenticator := authenticatorfactory.NewFromTokens(tokens, authn.APIAudiences)\n    authn.Authenticator = authenticatorunion.New(tokenAuthenticator, authn.Authenticator)\n}\n```\n\nThe loopback token authenticator is prepended to the standard authenticator chain, giving the internal API server client an identity in the `system:masters` group. This identity bypasses RBAC via the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` in the internal authorization chain (see \u00a710). The token is a random 256-bit bearer secret generated at startup and stored only in memory.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Request Parsing: Building the Authorization Context\n\n### 6.1 RequestInfo Structure\n\n`RequestInfo` (`requestinfo.go:44-74`) is a parsed representation of the HTTP request URL:\n\n```go\ntype RequestInfo struct {\n    IsResourceRequest bool    // true for /api/* and /apis/*\n    Path              string  // raw URL path\n    Verb              string  // kubernetes verb (create/get/list/watch/update/patch/delete/deletecollection/proxy)\n    APIPrefix         string  // \"api\" or \"apis\"\n    APIGroup          string  // \"\" (core), \"apps\", \"batch\", etc.\n    APIVersion        string  // \"v1\", \"v1beta1\", etc.\n    Namespace         string  // target namespace or \"\"\n    Resource          string  // \"pods\", \"deployments\", etc.\n    Subresource       string  // \"status\", \"log\", \"exec\", \"portforward\", etc.\n    Name              string  // specific object name\n    Parts             []string\n    FieldSelector     string  // unparsed (feature-gated)\n    LabelSelector     string  // unparsed (feature-gated)\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 URL Parsing Logic (`NewRequestInfo`, `requestinfo.go:129-277`)\n\nThe factory parses paths in a specific order that has security implications:\n\n**Verb mapping from HTTP method to Kubernetes verb:**\n\n| HTTP Method | K8s Verb (named resource) | K8s Verb (collection) |\n|---|---|---|\n| GET / HEAD | get | list |\n| GET ?watch=true | watch | watch |\n| POST | create | \u2014 |\n| PUT | update | \u2014 |\n| PATCH | patch | \u2014 |\n| DELETE | delete | deletecollection |\n\n**Special verb path prefixes** (`specialVerbs = {\"proxy\", \"watch\"}`): These consume a path segment. For example, `/api/v1/proxy/namespaces/ns/pods/foo` sets `Verb = \"proxy\"` and `Resource = \"pods\"`.\n\n**Subresource parsing** (`Parts[2]`): For a path like `/api/v1/namespaces/ns/pods/foo/exec`, `Parts = [\"pods\", \"foo\", \"exec\"]`, producing `Resource = \"pods\"`, `Name = \"foo\"`, `Subresource = \"exec\"`. Subresource matching in RBAC checks both exact resource/subresource combinations and wildcard `*/subresource` forms.\n\n**Selector propagation** (feature-gated `AuthorizeWithSelectors`): For `list`, `watch`, and `deletecollection` verbs, `fieldSelector` and `labelSelector` query parameters are stored unparsed in `RequestInfo` and lazily parsed when `GetFieldSelector()` / `GetLabelSelector()` are called on `AttributesRecord`.\n\n### 6.3 GetAuthorizerAttributes (`authorization.go:100-152`)\n\nThis function constructs the `AttributesRecord` used throughout the authorization phase:\n\n```go\nfunc GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx context.Context) (authorizer.Attributes, error) {\n    attribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{}\n\n    user, ok := request.UserFrom(ctx)\n    if ok { attribs.User = user }\n\n    requestInfo, found := request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx)\n    if !found { return nil, errors.New(\"no RequestInfo found in the context\") }\n\n    attribs.ResourceRequest = requestInfo.IsResourceRequest\n    attribs.Path            = requestInfo.Path\n    attribs.Verb            = requestInfo.Verb\n    attribs.APIGroup        = requestInfo.APIGroup\n    attribs.APIVersion      = requestInfo.APIVersion\n    attribs.Resource        = requestInfo.Resource\n    attribs.Subresource     = requestInfo.Subresource\n    attribs.Namespace       = requestInfo.Namespace\n    attribs.Name            = requestInfo.Name\n    // ... selector fields (feature-gated) ...\n    return &attribs, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe `AttributesRecord` is a **value type with no synchronization** \u2014 it is created fresh per request and never shared. The `GetFieldSelector()` and `GetLabelSelector()` accessors return pre-parsed values that are cached at construction time (the parsing happens in `GetAuthorizerAttributes()`, not lazily on the struct), making concurrent reads from multiple goroutines safe.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Impersonation: Identity Substitution Under Authorization Control\n\n### 7.1 WithImpersonation (`impersonation.go:41-183`)\n\nImpersonation allows an authenticated user to make requests on behalf of another identity. It is the primary mechanism used by CI/CD pipelines, controllers, and `kubectl --as`.\n\n**Trigger**: The presence of any impersonation header:\n- `Impersonate-User` (required if any other impersonation header is present)\n- `Impersonate-Group` (multi-value)\n- `Impersonate-Extra-<key>` (multi-value per key)\n- `Impersonate-Uid`\n\n**Security protocol** \u2014 for each requested impersonation target, before any substitution:\n\n```go\nactingAsAttributes := &authorizer.AttributesRecord{\n    User:            requestor,      // the ORIGINAL authenticated user\n    Verb:            \"impersonate\",  // special verb checked against RBAC rules\n    APIGroup:        gvk.Group,\n    Resource:        \"users\" | \"groups\" | \"serviceaccounts\" | \"userextras\" | \"uids\",\n    Name:            impersonationRequest.Name,\n    ResourceRequest: true,\n}\ndecision, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes)\nif err != nil || decision != authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    responsewriters.Forbidden(ctx, actingAsAttributes, w, req, reason, s)\n    return\n}\n```\n\nThe full authorizer chain is invoked for **each** impersonation element (user, each group, each extra key-value pair, UID). All must be individually authorized before the identity swap proceeds. A failure on any element causes an immediate 403 without processing any remaining elements.\n\n**Post-authorization identity construction**: After all impersonation elements are authorized, a `user.DefaultInfo` is constructed:\n\n```go\nnewUser := &user.DefaultInfo{\n    Name:   username,\n    Groups: groups,     // includes system:authenticated or system:unauthenticated as appropriate\n    Extra:  userExtra,\n    UID:    uid,\n}\nreq = req.WithContext(request.WithUser(ctx, newUser))\n```\n\n**Group normalization**: When impersonating a non-anonymous user and no groups are explicitly specified, `system:authenticated` is automatically appended. This prevents impersonation from accidentally creating an identity with fewer group memberships than expected by downstream policy.\n\n**Header cleanup**: All impersonation headers are deleted from the request before passing to the next handler, preventing double-impersonation or header leakage to the resource handler.\n\n**Audit logging**: `audit.LogImpersonatedUser(ae, newUser)` records both the original requestor and the impersonated identity on the audit event.\n\n---\n\n## 8. The Authorization Gate: WithAuthorization\n\n```go\n// authorization.go:57-98\nfunc withAuthorization(handler http.Handler, a authorizer.Authorizer, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer,\n    metrics recordAuthorizationMetricsFunc) http.Handler {\n    if a == nil {\n        klog.Warning(\"Authorization is disabled\")\n        return handler\n    }\n    return http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {\n        ctx := req.Context()\n        authorizationStart := time.Now()\n\n        attributes, err := GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)\n        if err != nil {\n            responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)\n            return\n        }\n        authorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n\n        authorizationFinish := time.Now()\n        defer func() {\n            metrics(ctx, authorized, err, authorizationStart, authorizationFinish)\n        }()\n\n        // Decision check precedes error check: an authorizer may return Allow with an error\n        if authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n            audit.AddAuditAnnotations(ctx,\n                decisionAnnotationKey, decisionAllow,\n                reasonAnnotationKey, reason)\n            handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n            return\n        }\n        if err != nil {\n            audit.AddAuditAnnotation(ctx, reasonAnnotationKey, reasonError)\n            responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)\n            return\n        }\n\n        // DecisionDeny or DecisionNoOpinion both reach here\n        audit.AddAuditAnnotations(ctx,\n            decisionAnnotationKey, decisionForbid,\n            reasonAnnotationKey, reason)\n        responsewriters.Forbidden(ctx, attributes, w, req, reason, s)\n    })\n}\n```\n\n**Key design decision**: The authorization decision is checked **before** the error. The comment explicitly acknowledges this: `\"an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request\"`. This means if the union authorizer returns `(DecisionAllow, reason, err)` \u2014 where the error came from a non-fatal resolution failure in a different sub-authorizer \u2014 the request is allowed. The error is not treated as a veto when a positive allow has been established.\n\n**Audit annotations**: Two annotations are written:\n- `authorization.k8s.io/decision`: `\"allow\"` or `\"forbid\"`\n- `authorization.k8s.io/reason`: human-readable explanation from the authorizer\n\nThese annotations appear in the audit event, enabling forensic analysis of why a request was allowed or denied.\n\n**Nil authorizer check**: If `a == nil`, authorization is completely disabled and a warning is logged. This is a valid configuration for development and testing but is insecure in production.\n\n---\n\n## 9. The Authorizer Chain: Union/Composite Dispatch\n\n```go\n// union.go:45-68\nfunc (authzHandler unionAuthzHandler) Authorize(ctx context.Context, a authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    var errlist    []error\n    var reasonlist []string\n\n    for _, currAuthzHandler := range authzHandler {\n        decision, reason, err := currAuthzHandler.Authorize(ctx, a)\n        if err != nil { errlist = append(errlist, err) }\n        if len(reason) != 0 { reasonlist = append(reasonlist, reason) }\n        switch decision {\n        case authorizer.DecisionAllow, authorizer.DecisionDeny:\n            return decision, reason, err   // short-circuit\n        case authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion:\n            // continue to next\n        }\n    }\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, strings.Join(reasonlist, \"\\n\"), utilerrors.NewAggregate(errlist)\n}\n```\n\n**Union semantics**:\n\n- **First Allow wins** and short-circuits the entire chain (no remaining authorizers are consulted).\n- **First Deny wins** and short-circuits the chain.\n- Only if **all** authorizers return `NoOpinion` does the aggregate return `NoOpinion`, which `WithAuthorization` maps to a 403.\n- Errors from individual authorizers are **collected but do not short-circuit** unless paired with `DecisionDeny`. An authorizer can return `(NoOpinion, reason, err)` and processing continues to the next authorizer.\n\n**Standard production chain** (typical kube-apiserver with `--authorization-mode=Node,RBAC`):\n\n```\nNode Authorizer \u2192 RBAC Authorizer \u2192 [Webhook Authorizer if configured]\n```\n\nEach wrapped by `InstrumentedAuthorizer` for metrics.\n\n**`RuleResolver` union** (`NewRuleResolvers`): A parallel union exists for `RulesFor()` queries (used by `SelfSubjectRulesReview`). This union **aggregates** (does not short-circuit) \u2014 it collects all rules from all resolvers.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Built-in Authorizers: alwaysAllow, alwaysDeny, privilegedGroup\n\n### 10.1 alwaysAllowAuthorizer\n\n```go\nfunc (alwaysAllowAuthorizer) Authorize(...) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, \"\", nil\n}\n```\n\nUsed in:\n- Test environments\n- `--authorization-mode=AlwaysAllow` (open access, insecure)\n- Single-node development clusters\n\n### 10.2 alwaysDenyAuthorizer\n\n```go\nfunc (alwaysDenyAuthorizer) Authorize(...) (decision authorizer.Decision, reason string, err error) {\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"Everything is forbidden.\", nil\n}\n```\n\n**Critical security observation**: Despite its name, `alwaysDenyAuthorizer` returns `DecisionNoOpinion`, **not** `DecisionDeny`. This means:\n\n- It does not short-circuit the union chain. If it were in a chain with another authorizer that returns `Allow`, the request would be **allowed**.\n- It is semantically a \"never allow\" (no-opinion authorizer) rather than an explicit deny.\n- The `RulesFor()` implementation returns an empty slice, making it indistinguishable from \"no rules\" rather than \"denied for all.\"\n\nThis is documented as intended for unit tests, but the semantic gap between the name and behavior is a potential source of confusion in custom authorization setups.\n\n### 10.3 privilegedGroupAuthorizer\n\n```go\nfunc (r *privilegedGroupAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attr authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    if attr.GetUser() == nil {\n        return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"Error\", errors.New(\"no user on request.\")\n    }\n    for _, attr_group := range attr.GetUser().GetGroups() {\n        for _, priv_group := range r.groups {\n            if priv_group == attr_group {\n                return authorizer.DecisionAllow, \"\", nil\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"\", nil\n}\n\n// Usage \u2014 NewPrivilegedGroups for loopback:\nfunc NewPrivilegedGroups(groups ...string) *privilegedGroupAuthorizer\n```\n\nUsed internally to grant unconditional access to specific groups. In the loopback authorization chain, it is configured with `user.SystemPrivilegedGroup` (`\"system:masters\"`), meaning any request carrying that group membership is immediately allowed without consulting RBAC. This is how the internal API server client (`system:apiserver`) bypasses policy checks.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Node Authorizer: Graph-Based Kubelet Restriction\n\n### 11.1 Architecture\n\n```go\n// node_authorizer.go:61-68\ntype NodeAuthorizer struct {\n    graph      *Graph              // in-memory node\u2192workload relationship graph\n    identifier nodeidentifier.NodeIdentifier\n    nodeRules  []rbacv1.PolicyRule // static rules for uniform node access\n    features   featuregate.FeatureGate\n}\n```\n\n### 11.2 Authorization Logic\n\n```go\nfunc (r *NodeAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attrs authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    nodeName, isNode := r.identifier.NodeIdentity(attrs.GetUser())\n    if !isNode { return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"\", nil }\n    if len(nodeName) == 0 {\n        return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, fmt.Sprintf(\"unknown node for user %q\", ...), nil\n    }\n    // resource-specific graph-based checks follow...\n}\n```\n\n**Identity check**: `NodeIdentity()` accepts a user only if:\n- Username prefix is `system:node:` (e.g. `system:node:worker-1`)\n- User belongs to `system:nodes` group\n\nIf either check fails, the node authorizer returns `NoOpinion` and the request proceeds to RBAC.\n\n**Graph-based checks** (for secrets, configmaps, PVCs, PVs, ResourceClaims): The in-memory graph encodes `node \u2192 pod \u2192 {secret, configmap, pvc \u2192 pv \u2192 secret, ResourceClaim}` edges. A kubelet can only access a secret or configmap if there is a graph path from the requesting node to that object. This prevents a compromised kubelet from reading secrets belonging to workloads scheduled on other nodes.\n\n**Static rule checks** (for uniform resources like nodes, leases, CSINodes): These are evaluated using `RulesAllow(attrs, r.nodeRules...)`, the same predicate used by RBAC, against a pre-defined set of `PolicyRule` objects.\n\n**Return values**: Node authorizer only returns `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion` \u2014 never `DecisionDeny`. A node making an out-of-scope request (e.g., accessing another node's secret) gets `NoOpinion`, which falls through to RBAC and then to a 403 if RBAC also has no applicable rules.\n\n---\n\n## 12. RBAC Authorizer: Core Policy Evaluation\n\n### 12.1 RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()\n\n```go\n// rbac.go:75-127\nfunc (r *RBACAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    ruleCheckingVisitor := &authorizingVisitor{requestAttributes: requestAttributes}\n\n    r.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(\n        ctx,\n        requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n        requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n        ruleCheckingVisitor.visit,\n    )\n\n    if ruleCheckingVisitor.allowed {\n        return authorizer.DecisionAllow, ruleCheckingVisitor.reason, nil\n    }\n\n    // Build denial log at verbosity 5\n    reason := \"\"\n    if len(ruleCheckingVisitor.errors) > 0 {\n        reason = fmt.Sprintf(\"RBAC: %v\", utilerrors.NewAggregate(ruleCheckingVisitor.errors))\n    }\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, reason, nil\n}\n```\n\n**The authorizingVisitor** (`rbac.go:55-73`):\n\n```go\ntype authorizingVisitor struct {\n    requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes\n    allowed bool\n    reason  string\n    errors  []error\n}\n\nfunc (v *authorizingVisitor) visit(source fmt.Stringer, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, err error) bool {\n    if rule != nil && RuleAllows(v.requestAttributes, rule) {\n        v.allowed = true\n        v.reason = fmt.Sprintf(\"RBAC: allowed by %s\", source.String())\n        return false  // stops iteration immediately\n    }\n    if err != nil {\n        v.errors = append(v.errors, err)\n    }\n    return true  // continue visiting\n}\n```\n\nThe visitor short-circuits on the **first matching rule**. It never evaluates all rules. The `source` string (e.g., `ClusterRoleBinding \"cluster-admin\" of ClusterRole \"cluster-admin\" to Group \"system:masters\"`) becomes the audit reason.\n\n**RBAC never returns `DecisionDeny`**: The only outcomes are `DecisionAllow` (a rule matched) or `DecisionNoOpinion` (no rule matched or all errors). An explicit RBAC deny is architecturally impossible \u2014 RBAC is a pure allowlist.\n\n### 12.2 DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()\n\n```go\n// rule.go:179-237\nfunc (r *DefaultRuleResolver) VisitRulesFor(ctx context.Context, user user.Info, namespace string,\n    visitor func(source fmt.Stringer, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, err error) bool) {\n\n    // Phase 1: ClusterRoleBindings (always evaluated; cluster-wide scope)\n    if clusterRoleBindings, err := r.clusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings(ctx); err != nil {\n        if !visitor(nil, nil, err) { return }\n    } else {\n        for _, clusterRoleBinding := range clusterRoleBindings {\n            subjectIndex, applies := appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")\n            if !applies { continue }\n            rules, err := r.GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, clusterRoleBinding.RoleRef, \"\")\n            if err != nil {\n                if !visitor(nil, nil, err) { return }\n                continue\n            }\n            for i := range rules {\n                if !visitor(sourceDescriber, &rules[i], nil) { return }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Phase 2: RoleBindings in namespace (only when namespace is non-empty)\n    if len(namespace) > 0 {\n        if roleBindings, err := r.roleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings(ctx, namespace); err != nil {\n            if !visitor(nil, nil, err) { return }\n        } else {\n            for _, roleBinding := range roleBindings {\n                subjectIndex, applies := appliesTo(user, roleBinding.Subjects, namespace)\n                if !applies { continue }\n                rules, err := r.GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, roleBinding.RoleRef, namespace)\n                if err != nil {\n                    if !visitor(nil, nil, err) { return }\n                    continue\n                }\n                for i := range rules {\n                    if !visitor(sourceDescriber, &rules[i], nil) { return }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Two-phase evaluation**:\n\n1. **Phase 1 \u2014 ClusterRoleBindings**: Always executed, regardless of namespace. A match here grants cluster-wide permission. `ClusterRole` rules fetched via `GetClusterRole()`.\n\n2. **Phase 2 \u2014 RoleBindings**: Executed only for namespaced requests (`namespace != \"\"`). A `RoleBinding` can reference either a `Role` (namespace-scoped rules) or a `ClusterRole` (but scoped to the namespace). Fetched via `GetRole()` or `GetClusterRole()` depending on `roleRef.Kind`.\n\n**Error handling philosophy**: Errors during `ListClusterRoleBindings`, `ListRoleBindings`, `GetRole`, or `GetClusterRole` are passed to the visitor as `(source, nil, err)`. The visitor may or may not stop iteration. In the `authorizingVisitor` used during authorization, errors are **collected** but do not stop processing. This is by design: RBAC is additive, and a partial rule set is still useful. A resource that would otherwise be allowed by an unresolvable binding will simply not be allowed by that binding \u2014 but other bindings continue to be evaluated.\n\n**No namespace escalation**: `VisitRulesFor` with a namespace only examines that namespace's role bindings. A `RoleBinding` in namespace A cannot grant permissions in namespace B.\n\n### 12.3 Subject Binding Matching: appliesTo / appliesToUser\n\n```go\n// rule.go:263-304\nfunc appliesTo(user user.Info, bindingSubjects []rbacv1.Subject, namespace string) (int, bool) {\n    for i, bindingSubject := range bindingSubjects {\n        if appliesToUser(user, bindingSubject, namespace) {\n            return i, true\n        }\n    }\n    return 0, false\n}\n\nfunc appliesToUser(user user.Info, subject rbacv1.Subject, namespace string) bool {\n    switch subject.Kind {\n    case rbacv1.UserKind:\n        return user.GetName() == subject.Name           // exact string match\n\n    case rbacv1.GroupKind:\n        return has(user.GetGroups(), subject.Name)      // linear scan of group list\n\n    case rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind:\n        saNamespace := namespace\n        if len(subject.Namespace) > 0 { saNamespace = subject.Namespace }\n        if len(saNamespace) == 0 { return false }\n        return serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())\n\n    default:\n        return false\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Three subject kinds**:\n\n- **`User`**: Exact string equality. Case-sensitive. No wildcard support.\n- **`Group`**: Linear membership check against `user.GetGroups()`. `system:authenticated` and `system:unauthenticated` are in this list by virtue of being added by the authenticator.\n- **`ServiceAccount`**: Uses `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(namespace, name, username)` which checks whether the username equals `system:serviceaccount:<namespace>:<name>`. Namespace defaults to the binding's namespace if the subject omits it.\n\nA `Subject.Kind` value that is not `User`, `Group`, or `ServiceAccount` silently returns `false`, making unknown subject types non-matching (safe default).\n\n### 12.4 Rule Predicate Evaluation: RuleAllows()\n\n```go\n// rbac.go:178-193\nfunc RuleAllows(requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n    if requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n        combinedResource := requestAttributes.GetResource()\n        if len(requestAttributes.GetSubresource()) > 0 {\n            combinedResource = requestAttributes.GetResource() + \"/\" + requestAttributes.GetSubresource()\n        }\n        return rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches(rule, requestAttributes.GetVerb()) &&\n               rbacv1helpers.APIGroupMatches(rule, requestAttributes.GetAPIGroup()) &&\n               rbacv1helpers.ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, requestAttributes.GetSubresource()) &&\n               rbacv1helpers.ResourceNameMatches(rule, requestAttributes.GetName())\n    }\n    return rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches(rule, requestAttributes.GetVerb()) &&\n           rbacv1helpers.NonResourceURLMatches(rule, requestAttributes.GetPath())\n}\n```\n\n**The four predicates for resource requests** (all must be true):\n\n**VerbMatches** (`evaluation_helpers.go:26-37`):\n```go\nfunc VerbMatches(rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, requestedVerb string) bool {\n    for _, ruleVerb := range rule.Verbs {\n        if ruleVerb == rbacv1.VerbAll { return true }   // wildcard \"*\"\n        if ruleVerb == requestedVerb  { return true }   // exact match\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\nMatches the wildcard `\"*\"` or an exact case-sensitive verb string. No partial matching or prefix matching.\n\n**APIGroupMatches** (`evaluation_helpers.go:39-50`):\n```go\nfunc APIGroupMatches(rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, requestedGroup string) bool {\n    for _, ruleGroup := range rule.APIGroups {\n        if ruleGroup == rbacv1.APIGroupAll { return true }  // wildcard \"*\"\n        if ruleGroup == requestedGroup     { return true }  // exact match\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\nNote: The core API group is the **empty string** `\"\"`, not `\"core\"`. A rule with `APIGroups: [\"\"]` matches core resources; `APIGroups: [\"*\"]` matches all groups.\n\n**ResourceMatches** (`evaluation_helpers.go:52-78`):\n```go\nfunc ResourceMatches(rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, combinedRequestedResource, requestedSubresource string) bool {\n    for _, ruleResource := range rule.Resources {\n        if ruleResource == rbacv1.ResourceAll { return true }    // \"*\"\n        if ruleResource == combinedRequestedResource { return true }  // \"pods/exec\" or \"pods\"\n        // Wildcard subresource: \"*/exec\"\n        if len(requestedSubresource) == 0 { continue }\n        if len(ruleResource) == len(requestedSubresource)+2 &&\n            strings.HasPrefix(ruleResource, \"*/\") &&\n            strings.HasSuffix(ruleResource, requestedSubresource) {\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\nThree matching patterns:\n1. Wildcard `\"*\"` \u2014 matches any resource or subresource\n2. Exact `\"pods/exec\"` \u2014 matches combined resource/subresource\n3. Wildcard subresource `\"*/exec\"` \u2014 matches the `exec` subresource of any resource\n\n**ResourceNameMatches** (`evaluation_helpers.go:80-92`):\n```go\nfunc ResourceNameMatches(rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, requestedName string) bool {\n    if len(rule.ResourceNames) == 0 { return true }  // no name restriction = matches all\n    for _, ruleName := range rule.ResourceNames {\n        if ruleName == requestedName { return true }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\nEmpty `ResourceNames` in the rule means \"any name.\" A non-empty list restricts to those exact names. No wildcard support in `ResourceNames`.\n\n**NonResourceURLMatches** (`evaluation_helpers.go:94-108`):\n```go\nfunc NonResourceURLMatches(rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule, requestedURL string) bool {\n    for _, ruleURL := range rule.NonResourceURLs {\n        if ruleURL == rbacv1.NonResourceAll { return true }   // \"*\"\n        if ruleURL == requestedURL           { return true }   // exact\n        if strings.HasSuffix(ruleURL, \"*\") && strings.HasPrefix(requestedURL, strings.TrimRight(ruleURL, \"*\")) {\n            return true  // prefix wildcard: \"/metrics/*\"\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\nOnly supports prefix-wildcard (suffix `\"*\"`), not arbitrary glob patterns.\n\n### 12.5 Policy Comparator and ConfirmNoEscalation\n\n```go\n// rule.go:52-89\nfunc ConfirmNoEscalation(ctx context.Context, ruleResolver AuthorizationRuleResolver, rules []rbacv1.PolicyRule) error {\n    user, ok := genericapirequest.UserFrom(ctx)\n    namespace, _ := genericapirequest.NamespaceFrom(ctx)\n\n    ownerRules, err := ruleResolver.RulesFor(ctx, user, namespace)\n    // err is non-fatal (partial rules are still evaluated)\n\n    ownerRightsCover, missingRights := validation.Covers(ownerRules, rules)\n    if !ownerRightsCover {\n        // return error listing the specific missing privileges\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"user %q (groups=%q) is attempting to grant RBAC permissions not currently held:\\n%s\", ...)\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n`ConfirmNoEscalation` is called during `create` and `update` operations on `Role`, `ClusterRole`, `RoleBinding`, and `ClusterRoleBinding` objects. It prevents privilege escalation via role creation by verifying that all rules in the role being created or modified are a **subset** of the requesting user's own current permissions.\n\n**The `Covers()` algorithm** (`policy_comparator.go:27-53`):\n\n1. Decompose all `servantRules` (rules to be granted) into atomic tuples via `BreakdownRule()`: each tuple has at most one verb, one resource, one group, one resourceName.\n2. For each atomic tuple, check if any `ownerRule` covers it via `ruleCovers()`.\n3. Return `true` only if every atomic tuple is covered.\n\n**`ruleCovers()` logic** (`policy_comparator.go:158-173`):\n- `verbMatches`: owner rule has `\"*\"` or has the specific verb\n- `groupMatches`: owner rule has `\"*\"` or the specific group\n- `resourceMatches`: via `resourceCoversAll()` \u2014 supports `\"*\"`, exact match, and `\"*/subresource\"` wildcards\n- `resourceNameMatches`: if servant has no specific names, owner must also have no name restriction; if servant has specific names, owner must have no restriction or must include all those names\n- `nonResourceURLMatches`: via `nonResourceURLsCoversAll()` \u2014 supports prefix wildcards\n\nAll four must be true for coverage. This prevents a user from creating a rule that grants `delete pods` when they only hold `get pods`.\n\n**Escalation bypass for `system:masters`**: A user in `system:masters` is allowed by `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` before reaching RBAC admission. The `ConfirmNoEscalation` check is an admission controller, not an authorization check, so it runs in the resource handler. However, users in `system:masters` can be granted bypass of escalation checks via the `rbac.authorization.kubernetes.io/autoupdate` annotation and the `--authorization-rbac-rules-cache-ttl` flag.\n\n---\n\n## 13. Webhook Authorizer: External Policy Delegation\n\n### 13.1 Structure\n\n```go\n// webhook.go:72-82\ntype WebhookAuthorizer struct {\n    subjectAccessReview subjectAccessReviewer  // HTTP client to remote endpoint\n    responseCache       *cache.LRUExpireCache  // 8192-entry LRU cache\n    authorizedTTL       time.Duration          // separate TTL for allowed responses\n    unauthorizedTTL     time.Duration          // separate TTL for denied/no-opinion responses\n    retryBackoff        wait.Backoff           // exponential backoff on transient errors\n    decisionOnError     authorizer.Decision    // what to return on connectivity failure\n    celMatcher          *authorizationcel.CELMatcher  // match conditions (feature-gated)\n    name                string\n}\n```\n\n### 13.2 Authorize() Flow\n\n```go\n// webhook.go:188-298\nfunc (w *WebhookAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attr authorizer.Attributes) (decision authorizer.Decision, reason string, err error) {\n    // 1. Build SubjectAccessReview request\n    r := &authorizationv1.SubjectAccessReview{}\n    r.Spec = authorizationv1.SubjectAccessReviewSpec{\n        User:   user.GetName(),\n        UID:    user.GetUID(),\n        Groups: user.GetGroups(),\n        Extra:  convertToSARExtra(user.GetExtra()),\n    }\n    if attr.IsResourceRequest() {\n        r.Spec.ResourceAttributes = resourceAttributesFrom(attr)\n    } else {\n        r.Spec.NonResourceAttributes = &authorizationv1.NonResourceAttributes{...}\n    }\n\n    // 2. CEL match conditions (StructuredAuthorizationConfiguration feature gate)\n    if utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(genericfeatures.StructuredAuthorizationConfiguration) {\n        matches, err := w.match(ctx, r)\n        if err != nil { return w.decisionOnError, \"\", err }\n        if !matches   { return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"\", nil }\n    }\n\n    // 3. Cache lookup\n    key, _ := json.Marshal(r.Spec)\n    if entry, ok := w.responseCache.Get(string(key)); ok {\n        r.Status = entry.(authorizationv1.SubjectAccessReviewStatus)\n    } else {\n        // 4. Remote call with exponential backoff and retry\n        result, statusCode, sarErr = w.subjectAccessReview.Create(ctx, r, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n        // 5. Cache response\n        if r.Status.Allowed {\n            w.responseCache.Add(string(key), r.Status, w.authorizedTTL)\n        } else {\n            w.responseCache.Add(string(key), r.Status, w.unauthorizedTTL)\n        }\n    }\n\n    // 6. Map SAR status to Decision\n    switch {\n    case r.Status.Denied && r.Status.Allowed:\n        return authorizer.DecisionDeny, r.Status.Reason, fmt.Errorf(\"both allow and deny\")\n    case r.Status.Denied:  return authorizer.DecisionDeny, r.Status.Reason, nil\n    case r.Status.Allowed: return authorizer.DecisionAllow, r.Status.Reason, nil\n    default:               return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, r.Status.Reason, nil\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Webhook is the only standard authorizer that can return `DecisionDeny`** (when the remote endpoint sets `status.denied: true`). This enables external policy engines (OPA, Gatekeeper, custom webhooks) to implement explicit deny rules.\n\n**Cache key**: The entire `SubjectAccessReviewSpec` serialized as JSON. The cache is per-instance (not shared across API server replicas). Cache entries for allowed and denied responses use separate TTLs, allowing operators to tune aggressiveness differently.\n\n**`decisionOnError`**: Configurable behavior on webhook failure. Options:\n- `NoOpinion` \u2014 fail open (default for backwards compatibility; the TODO comment in the code notes this)\n- `Deny` \u2014 fail closed (more secure, but risks locking out all access if the webhook is unavailable)\n\n**CEL match conditions** (`StructuredAuthorizationConfiguration` feature gate): Pre-filter expressions evaluated before the cache lookup and remote call. If any condition evaluates to `false`, the webhook is skipped entirely (`NoOpinion`). If a condition evaluation returns an error, `decisionOnError` is applied. This allows selective webhook dispatch based on request attributes, reducing webhook load and latency for common cases.\n\n**Selector propagation**: When `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is enabled, field selectors and label selectors are included in `SubjectAccessReview.Spec.ResourceAttributes`, allowing the webhook to make more granular decisions (e.g., allowing `list pods` only for pods with `labelSelector: app=myapp`).\n\n---\n\n## 14. Bootstrap Policy and Privileged Identities\n\n### 14.1 cluster-admin ClusterRole\n\n```go\n// bootstrappolicy/policy.go:214-222\n{\n    ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: \"cluster-admin\"},\n    Rules: []rbacv1.PolicyRule{\n        rbacv1helpers.NewRule(\"*\").Groups(\"*\").Resources(\"*\").RuleOrDie(),\n        rbacv1helpers.NewRule(\"*\").URLs(\"*\").RuleOrDie(),\n    },\n}\n```\n\nThis role grants all verbs on all API groups and resources (both resource and non-resource URLs). Any subject bound to this role via `ClusterRoleBinding` has unrestricted access to the entire API.\n\n### 14.2 system:masters Binding\n\n```go\n// bootstrappolicy/policy.go:635\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"cluster-admin\").Groups(user.SystemPrivilegedGroup).BindingOrDie()\n```\n\n`system:masters` group \u2192 `cluster-admin` ClusterRole. Any user whose `user.Info.Groups` contains `\"system:masters\"` is cluster-admin via RBAC policy. Additionally, the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` in the loopback chain short-circuits before RBAC, so `system:masters` gets allowed at two independent levels.\n\n### 14.3 Other Default Bindings\n\n```go\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:monitoring\").Groups(user.MonitoringGroup).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:discovery\").Groups(user.AllAuthenticated).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:basic-user\").Groups(user.AllAuthenticated).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:public-info-viewer\").Groups(user.AllAuthenticated, user.AllUnauthenticated).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:node-proxier\").Users(user.KubeProxy).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:kube-controller-manager\").Users(user.KubeControllerManager).BindingOrDie()\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:kube-scheduler\").Users(user.KubeScheduler).BindingOrDie()\n```\n\nNotable security implications:\n- **`system:discovery`** and **`system:basic-user`** are bound to `system:authenticated`, meaning every authenticated user can create `SelfSubjectAccessReview` and discover API groups/versions. This is a deliberate usability feature.\n- **`system:public-info-viewer`** is bound to both authenticated and unauthenticated users, allowing unauthenticated access to `/livez`, `/readyz`, `/healthz`, `/version`, etc.\n- **`system:kube-dns`** is bound to service account `kube-system/kube-dns`.\n\n---\n\n## 15. Audit Instrumentation of Authorization Decisions\n\nThe audit system captures authorization outcomes at multiple points:\n\n### 15.1 WithAudit filter\n\n`WithAudit` (`audit.go`) wraps the `ResponseWriter` to capture HTTP status codes, and sends `RequestReceived` and `ResponseComplete` audit events according to the configured audit policy. Audit events carry a `stage` field:\n\n- `RequestReceived` \u2014 emitted immediately when the request arrives at the audit filter (before authorization)\n- `ResponseStarted` \u2014 for long-running requests (watch, exec, port-forward)\n- `ResponseComplete` \u2014 emitted after the response is fully sent\n\n### 15.2 Authorization Annotations\n\n`WithAuthorization` writes two annotations to the current audit event:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    decisionAnnotationKey = \"authorization.k8s.io/decision\"   // \"allow\" or \"forbid\"\n    reasonAnnotationKey   = \"authorization.k8s.io/reason\"     // authorizer reason string\n)\n```\n\nThese appear in the structured audit log as:\n```json\n\"annotations\": {\n  \"authorization.k8s.io/decision\": \"allow\",\n  \"authorization.k8s.io/reason\": \"RBAC: allowed by ClusterRoleBinding \\\"cluster-admin\\\" of ClusterRole \\\"cluster-admin\\\" to Group \\\"system:masters\\\"\"\n}\n```\n\n### 15.3 Authentication Failure Audit\n\n`WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` wraps the `Unauthorized` handler and emits a `ResponseComplete` audit event with `responseCode: 401` before the 401 response is sent.\n\n### 15.4 Impersonation Audit\n\n`audit.LogImpersonatedUser(ae, newUser)` adds the impersonated identity to the audit event, so log entries show both the original requestor and the impersonated identity.\n\n---\n\n## 16. Metrics: InstrumentedAuthorizer\n\n```go\n// metrics.go:62-91\nfunc InstrumentedAuthorizer(authorizerType string, authorizerName string, delegate authorizer.Authorizer) authorizer.Authorizer {\n    RegisterMetrics()\n    return &instrumentedAuthorizer{authorizerType, authorizerName, delegate}\n}\n\nfunc (a *instrumentedAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attributes authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    decision, reason, err := a.delegate.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n    switch decision {\n    case authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion:\n        // non-terminal, not recorded in counter\n    case authorizer.DecisionAllow:\n        RecordAuthorizationDecision(a.authorizerType, a.authorizerName, \"allowed\")\n    case authorizer.DecisionDeny:\n        RecordAuthorizationDecision(a.authorizerType, a.authorizerName, \"denied\")\n    }\n    return decision, reason, err\n}\n```\n\n**Metric name**: `apiserver_authorization_decisions_total`\n\n**Labels**: `{type=\"RBAC|Node|Webhook|...\", name=\"<authorizer-name>\", decision=\"allowed|denied\"}`\n\n**Stability level**: `ALPHA` \u2014 subject to change without notice.\n\n**Design implication**: `DecisionNoOpinion` is **not recorded** as a metric observation. This means the counter only tracks **terminal** decisions (decisions that stopped the chain). A high `allowed` count on RBAC and zero `denied` count on Node or Webhook does not mean those authorizers are never consulted \u2014 they may be returning `NoOpinion` for every request without any metric evidence.\n\n---\n\n## 17. Loopback / API Server Internal Clients\n\n### 17.1 Token Registration\n\nAt startup, `AuthorizeClientBearerToken()` creates an in-memory bearer token for internal use:\n\n```go\ntokens[privilegedLoopbackToken] = &user.DefaultInfo{\n    Name:   user.APIServerUser,              // \"system:apiserver\"\n    UID:    uid,                             // random UUID; changes per restart\n    Groups: []string{user.AllAuthenticated, user.SystemPrivilegedGroup},\n}\n```\n\nThe token is a random secret stored in `loopback.BearerToken` (a `*restclient.Config`). It is prepended to the authenticator chain so it is checked before any external authenticator.\n\n### 17.2 Authorization Path\n\nThe loopback authorization chain uses `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` configured with `system:masters`:\n\n```\nprivilegedGroupAuthorizer(system:masters)  \u2192  [other authorizers]\n```\n\nSince `system:apiserver` is in `system:masters`, **every loopback request is authorized by the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` before RBAC is consulted**. The loopback client effectively bypasses all RBAC policy.\n\n---\n\n## 18. \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n---\n\n## 19. Security Findings and Analysis\n\n### Finding 1: RBAC is Allowlist-Only \u2014 No Explicit Deny Semantics\n\n**Location**: `rbac.go:75-127`, `union.go:60-66`\n\n**Description**: RBAC never returns `DecisionDeny`. It can only return `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion`. An explicit deny in RBAC policy is architecturally impossible.\n\n**Implication**: In a `Node \u2192 RBAC` chain with no webhook:\n- A request is allowed if **any** ClusterRoleBinding or RoleBinding grants the required permission.\n- A request is denied only if **no** binding grants the permission.\n- There is no way to use RBAC to revoke a permission granted by a higher-priority binding.\n\nFor example, if `cluster-admin` ClusterRoleBinding applies to a user, there is no RBAC-level mechanism to selectively deny that user access to a specific resource. Denial requires either removing the binding entirely, or adding a Webhook authorizer that can return `DecisionDeny`.\n\n**Risk**: Over-privileged bindings cannot be narrowed through deny rules. Least-privilege enforcement relies entirely on correct binding scope.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 2: alwaysDenyAuthorizer Returns NoOpinion, Not Deny\n\n**Location**: `authorizerfactory/builtin.go:60-61`\n\n**Description**:\n```go\nfunc (alwaysDenyAuthorizer) Authorize(...) (decision authorizer.Decision, reason string, err error) {\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"Everything is forbidden.\", nil\n}\n```\n\nDespite its name, `alwaysDenyAuthorizer` does not produce `DecisionDeny`. If placed before an `alwaysAllow` authorizer in the chain, requests would still be allowed.\n\n**Risk**: Any system that constructs an authorization chain and relies on `alwaysDenyAuthorizer` to provide guaranteed denial for certain requests (e.g., as a deny override) is silently incorrect. The semantic gap between the name and behavior is a correctness risk for custom authorization chains.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 3: Authorization Precedes Error Handling in WithAuthorization\n\n**Location**: `authorization.go:78-85`\n\n**Description**:\n```go\n// an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request\nif authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n    return\n}\nif err != nil {\n    responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)\n    return\n}\n```\n\nIf the union authorizer returns `(DecisionAllow, reason, err)`, the request is allowed even if there was an error in a sub-authorizer. This is intentional \u2014 RBAC errors (e.g., failure to list a specific binding) are non-fatal when another binding already granted access. However, it means the error is silently swallowed from the caller's perspective.\n\n**Risk**: Transient errors in authorization (e.g., etcd read failures) combined with an allow from a different binding are invisible in the HTTP response path. They are accessible only through audit annotations and logs. An operator reviewing HTTP traffic patterns would not see these errors.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 4: Partial Rule Resolution Does Not Abort Authorization\n\n**Location**: `rule.go:179-237`\n\n**Description**: Errors from `GetRoleReferenceRules()` (e.g., a `RoleBinding` referencing a deleted `Role`) are passed to the visitor as `(nil_source, nil_rule, err)`. The visitor collects the error but continues processing remaining bindings. As a result, a binding referencing a non-existent role silently provides no permissions, while all other bindings continue to be evaluated.\n\n**Risk**: A deleted role does not cause immediate authorization failures for requests that would have been denied only by that role \u2014 other bindings can still grant access. This is the correct behavior for an additive policy model, but it means that orphaned `RoleBinding` objects (pointing to deleted `Role`/`ClusterRole`) silently fail without alerting administrators. The error is visible only in verbose logs (`klog.V(5)`) and in the `reason` field of the authorization response (only when RBAC is the sole denying factor).\n\n---\n\n### Finding 5: system:masters Group Provides Two Independent Bypass Paths\n\n**Location**: `authorizerfactory/builtin.go:72-91`, `bootstrappolicy/policy.go:635`\n\n**Description**: The `system:masters` group grants cluster-admin access through two independent mechanisms:\n1. **`privilegedGroupAuthorizer`**: In the loopback authorization chain, this authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` for any user in `system:masters` before RBAC is consulted.\n2. **Bootstrap ClusterRoleBinding**: `cluster-admin` ClusterRoleBinding binds `system:masters` group, granting unconditional access through the RBAC path.\n\n**Risk**: Compromising any credential that places a user in `system:masters` (client certificate with `O=system:masters`, loopback bearer token) provides complete cluster access. There is no revocation mechanism short of certificate rotation or API server restart (for the loopback token). The group cannot be \"un-bound\" from `cluster-admin` because the bootstrap reconciliation would re-create the binding.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 6: Webhook Fail-Open Default and Cache Poisoning Risk\n\n**Location**: `webhook.go:185-187`, `webhook.go:280-286`\n\n**Description**: The webhook authorizer defaults to `decisionOnError = DecisionNoOpinion` (fail-open). On connectivity failure:\n```go\n// we're returning NoOpinion, and the parent context has not timed out or been canceled\nif w.decisionOnError == authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion && ctx.Err() == nil {\n    w.metrics.RecordWebhookFailOpen(ctx, w.name, metricsResult)\n}\nreturn w.decisionOnError, \"\", err\n```\n\nThe `WebhookFailOpen` metric is recorded, but the request continues to be evaluated by subsequent authorizers (if any) or falls through to 403 if the webhook was the last authorizer. If the chain is `RBAC \u2192 Webhook`, RBAC already returned `NoOpinion` (no rule applied), so webhook failure results in 403 \u2014 fail-closed by accident. If the chain is `Webhook \u2192 RBAC`, webhook failure means RBAC decides alone.\n\n**Cache key concern**: The LRU cache key is `json.Marshal(r.Spec)` \u2014 the entire `SubjectAccessReviewSpec`. This includes user name, groups, extra attributes, and the full resource attributes. Cache entries can persist for `authorizedTTL` or `unauthorizedTTL` after the original policy decision was made. If RBAC rules change (e.g., a binding is deleted), the webhook cache may still serve the old authorization decision until TTL expiry.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 7: RequestInfo Parsing Determines Verb \u2014 HTTP Method is Not Final\n\n**Location**: `requestinfo.go:165-258`\n\n**Description**: The Kubernetes verb used for authorization is not simply the HTTP method. The parser applies several transformations:\n- `GET` on a collection (`/api/v1/pods`) \u2192 `list`\n- `GET` with `?watch=true` \u2192 `watch`\n- `DELETE` on a collection \u2192 `deletecollection`\n- Path prefix `proxy` \u2192 verb `proxy`\n- Path prefix `watch` \u2192 verb `watch`\n\n**Risk**: A RBAC rule granting `get pods` does not grant `list pods` or `watch pods`. These are three distinct verbs requiring three distinct grants. Operators who grant `get` expecting it to cover all read operations will find `list` and `watch` are denied. Conversely, `list` grants the ability to enumerate all pod names \u2014 which may have information-disclosure implications even without `get` on individual pods.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 8: Impersonation Requires Per-Element Authorization\n\n**Location**: `impersonation.go:71-123`\n\n**Description**: Each element of an impersonation request (user, each group, each extra key/value pair, UID) is individually authorized. The authorization uses `Verb: \"impersonate\"` against the resource type (`users`, `groups`, `serviceaccounts`, `userextras`, `uids`).\n\n**Risk**: A user with permission to `impersonate users` but not `impersonate groups` cannot fully impersonate a service account (which requires both user and group impersonation). The check is fine-grained. However, the `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers are not validated for content beyond URL-safe characters. Extra attributes can carry arbitrary data that downstream authorization webhooks may use for policy decisions \u2014 an attacker with impersonation rights could inject arbitrary extra attributes to influence webhook policy.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 9: Selector-Based Authorization is Feature-Gated\n\n**Location**: `authorization.go:125-149`, `requestinfo.go:261-275`\n\n**Description**: The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate controls whether `fieldSelector` and `labelSelector` query parameters are included in `AttributesRecord` and forwarded to webhook authorizers. When disabled (default in older versions), selectors are ignored for authorization purposes.\n\n**Implication**: A webhook authorizer cannot distinguish between `list pods` and `list pods?labelSelector=app=critical` unless the feature gate is enabled. Without the feature gate, the two requests are authorization-equivalent. Operators relying on webhook policies scoped to specific selectors must ensure this gate is enabled.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 10: Anonymous User Access to Health and Discovery Endpoints\n\n**Location**: `bootstrappolicy/policy.go:639`\n\n```go\nrbacv1helpers.NewClusterBinding(\"system:public-info-viewer\").Groups(user.AllAuthenticated, user.AllUnauthenticated).BindingOrDie()\n```\n\nThe `system:public-info-viewer` ClusterRole is bound to `system:unauthenticated`, granting unauthenticated access to `/livez`, `/readyz`, `/healthz`, and `/version`. This is intentional for liveness and readiness probe scenarios but exposes the Kubernetes version string to unauthenticated callers, which may assist in reconnaissance.\n\n---\n\n## 20. Summary of Security Properties\n\n| Property | Value | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| Authorization model | Additive allowlist | No deny rules in RBAC; only explicit allow or no-opinion |\n| Deny mechanism | Union short-circuit or webhook `status.denied` | Only webhook can explicitly deny |\n| RBAC decision on no match | `DecisionNoOpinion` (\u2192 403) | Not `DecisionDeny`; semantically identical outcome in standard chains |\n| Error handling | Non-fatal; partial evaluation continues | Deleted roles silently provide no permissions |\n| system:masters | Two bypass paths (privilegedGroupAuthorizer + cluster-admin binding) | Irrevocable without restart or cert rotation |\n| Impersonation gating | Full authorizer chain called per impersonation element | Correctly gates on original identity |\n| Audit coverage | RequestReceived before authz; annotations after authz | Both allow and deny decisions are audited |\n| Metrics | Terminal decisions only (Allow/Deny); NoOpinion not counted | Can undercount authorization activity |\n| Webhook failure mode | Configurable; default NoOpinion (fail-open) | Metric `WebhookFailOpen` recorded |\n| Webhook cache | Per-instance LRU (8192 entries); separate TTL for allow/deny | Policy changes not reflected until TTL expiry |\n| Verb mapping | HTTP method \u2192 k8s verb (not 1:1) | `get` \u2260 `list` \u2260 `watch`; `delete` \u2192 `deletecollection` for collections |\n| Anonymous access | Allowed to health/version endpoints by default | Exposes Kubernetes version string |\n| Selector authorization | Feature-gated (`AuthorizeWithSelectors`) | Off by default in older releases |\n| Privilege escalation prevention | `ConfirmNoEscalation()` in admission | Users cannot grant more rights than they hold |\n| HTTP/2 anonymous DoS mitigation | Feature-gated (`UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation`) | Forces `Connection: close` for anonymous HTTP/2 |\n",
  "path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"
